**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. ### **Area 1: Economic & Trade Policy**

**Topic 1.1: Administration Implements Sweeping New Global Tariffs**

The Trump administration is executing a significant realignment of U.S. trade policy, centered on a new executive order imposing global tariff rates effective August 7 [1]. This action, which delayed the previous deadline, has injected a fresh wave of uncertainty into the global economy [2]. Core to the new policy is a steep 40% duty on all transshipped goods, designed to counter circumvention [3]. The White House has released a comprehensive list of new rates for dozens of countries, resulting in a "tariff shock" for key partners. Switzerland, for example, now faces an unexpected 39% U.S. tariff, highlighting the disruptive scale of the changes [4].

**DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**
**July 26, 2025**

**OVERVIEW**

This briefing synthesizes intelligence from today’s news cycle to provide an objective, non-partisan analysis of the most urgent political, economic, and national security developments. The administration is advancing a disruptive trade agenda with significant global and domestic repercussions. Simultaneously, intense friction is developing between the executive and judicial branches, while new political movements and shifting alliances are reshaping the 2025 landscape. Congressional action and oversight are critical across multiple fronts.

---

### **Area 1: Economic & Trade Policy**

**Topic 1.1: Administration Implements Sweeping New Global Tariffs**

The Trump administration is executing a significant realignment of U.S. trade policy, centered on a new executive order imposing global tariff rates effective August 7 [1]. This action, which delayed the previous deadline, has injected a fresh wave of uncertainty into the global economy [2]. Core to the new policy is a steep 40% duty on all transshipped goods, designed to counter circumvention [3]. The White House has released a comprehensive list of new rates for dozens of countries, resulting in a "tariff shock" for key partners. Switzerland, for example, now faces an unexpected 39% U.S. tariff, highlighting the disruptive scale of the changes [4]. One major editorial board has characterized the new tariff regime as "both a political and an economic threat" [5].

**References:**
[1] Trump issues order imposing new global tariff rates effective Aug. 7, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/07/31/trump-executive-order-higher-tariff-rates-00487913

[2] Trump injects new dose of uncertainty in tariffs as he pushes start date back to Aug. 7, https://apnews.com/article/trump-tariffs-effect-05bc12428163b9f28ef80f952cf9dafd

[3] Trump rejigs tariff rates ahead of deadline, levies 40% duties on all transshipped goods, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/08/01/trump-rejigs-tariff-rates-ahead-of-deadline-levies-40percent-duties-on-all-transshipped-goods.html

[4] Switzerland’s tariff shock: The 39% U.S. hit no one saw coming, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/08/01/switzerland-economic-blow-with-surprise-39percent-us-tariff.html

[5] The Guardian view on Trump’s tariffs: both a political and an economic threat, https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2025/jul/31/the-guardian-view-on-trumps-tariffs-both-a-political-and-an-economic-threat

**Topic 1.2: U.S. Economic Indicators Point to Slowdown**

Recent economic data indicates a cooling labor market, with the U.S. economy adding a disappointing 73,000 jobs in July, according to multiple reports [1, 2]. This weak jobs report coincides with reporting that indicates a segment of voters and businesses feel the administration's aggressive trade policies have not yet delivered the promised results, expressing that they are still "wanting more" [3]. While the direct economic impact is still unfolding, these indicators suggest growing headwinds.

**References:**
[1] Employers Pulled Back on Hiring, Adding 73,000 Jobs, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/08/01/us/politics/jobs-report-us-economy.html?smid=nytcore-ios-share&referringSource=articleShare

[2] The US economy added just 73,000 jobs in July, https://www.cnn.com/2025/08/01/economy/us-jobs-report-july

[3] Trump trade wins leave voters, businesses wanting more, https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/5430702-trump-trade-deals-approval-drop/

**Topic 1.3: Domestic Economic Directives Advance Amid Scrutiny**

President Trump is pursuing several specific domestic economic initiatives through direct executive pressure. He has issued a public demand for pharmaceutical companies to lower drug prices within the United States while simultaneously raising them in other countries [1]. In a separate policy push, the "No Tax on Tips" slogan is being characterized in at least one outlet as an "industry plant" rather than a grassroots proposal [2]. On retirement policy, one analysis argues that the administration’s proposed “‘Trump Accounts’ Cannot Possibly Replace Social Security” [3].

**References:**
[1] Trump demands drug companies lower prices in U.S. and raise them in other countries, https://www.theglobeandmail.com/business/article-trump-demands-drug-companies-lower-prices-in-us-and-raise-them-in/

### **Area 2: Foreign Policy & National Security**

**Topic 2.1: U.S.-Canada Trade War Escalates Sharply**

Trade tensions with Canada have escalated into a critical diplomatic conflict, with the White House increasing the tariff on all Canadian goods to 35% [1]. At least one report directly links the tariff hike to Canada's foreign policy stance on Palestine [2], while another notes the administration officially cited fentanyl trafficking as justification for raising the rate from a previous 25% [3]. This punitive action against Canada was pointedly contrasted with a "reprieve" on tariffs reportedly given to Mexico, signaling a complex and volatile use of trade as a foreign policy weapon [4]. Canada's Prime Minister Mark Carney has officially stated his government is "disappointed" by the move [5].

**References:**
[1] Trump increases tariff on Canada to 35%, White House says, https://www.reuters.com/business/trump-increases-tariff-canada-35-white-house-says-2025-07-31/

[3] Trump increases tariff on Canada to 35% from 25%, cites fentanyl, https://www.ctvnews.ca/business/article/trump-increases-tariff-on-canada-to-35-from-25-cites-fentanyl/

**Topic 2.2: Potential for U.S.-China Trade Deal Emerges**

Amid broad trade conflicts, a positive signal has emerged regarding U.S.-China relations. Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent has publicly stated, “we have the makings of a deal’ with China” [1]. The available headlines do not provide any further specifics on the content, timing, or certainty of this potential agreement, but the statement marks a notable development.

**Topic 2.3: Shifting Dynamics in Middle East Policy**

The administration is navigating a complex Middle East policy, balancing a new aid initiative for Gaza against public remarks on U.S.-Israel policy that are being described as "mixed messaging" [1]. The White House has signaled President Trump’s intent to approve a new Gaza aid plan, with the announcement pending a visit from an individual identified only as Witkoff [2]. Concurrently, within Congress, a progressive faction including Rep. Ro Khanna is actively campaigning for official U.S. recognition of a Palestinian state, adding a new dimension to the domestic debate [3].

**References:**

**Topic 2.4: Major Defense Contract Awarded Amid Alliance Tensions**

In a significant defense procurement move, the U.S. Army has awarded a $10 billion contract to the technology company Palantir [1]. This deal is being reported as part of a broader pattern of the company expanding its reach "even further into government" [2]. Separately, U.S. Senators are reportedly taking legislative action to replace missile stockpiles that were used in attacks against Houthi targets authorized by the Trump administration [3].

### **Area 3: Executive Branch & Domestic Policy**

**Topic 3.1: White House Faces Staffing Turmoil and Scrutiny**

Reports indicate a high level of staff turmoil at the White House, with a surge in firings attributed to internal questions regarding staffers' loyalty to the President [1]. This activity is being characterized by some as a deliberate effort by President Trump to "purge Musk’s mark on government" [2]. Separately, the administration has announced a major and costly renovation project: the construction of a new $200 million, golden ballroom in the East Wing as part of a "modernized" White House makeover [3, 4].

**Topic 3.2: Immigration Enforcement Efforts Intensify**

The administration is significantly intensifying immigration enforcement nationwide. Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) reports that its hiring is ramping up, with over 1,000 tentative job offers already made to new personnel [1]. In a significant supporting measure, the National Guard has been ordered to assist ICE with paperwork processing at immigration facilities, freeing up enforcement agents for field operations [2]. This federal push is having downstream effects; in one example, New York's Eric Adams is facing criticism that his recent veto of a bill concerning unlicensed vendors aids the administration's broader immigration crackdown [3].

**References:**

**Topic 3.3: Sweeping Social and Regulatory Changes Pursued by Executive Order**

The administration is advancing a broad social and regulatory agenda through executive action. One of the most significant initiatives is a reported bid to "scrap almost all pollution regulations," a move with profound environmental and economic implications [1]. In a separate policy affecting the federal workforce, the administration has affirmed that government employees are permitted to encourage their co-workers to "re-think" their religious beliefs [2]. Other executive actions have drawn criticism, with one order described as "criminalizing houselessness" [3], while another reinstates the Presidential Fitness Test for school children [4].

### **Area 4: Justice System, Investigations, & Legal Controversies**

**Topic 4.1: Epstein Case Fallout Continues to Roil Administration**

The Jeffrey Epstein case remains a major source of political and legal crises. President Trump's recent comment that Epstein had "stole" accuser Virginia Giuffre from Mar-a-Lago elicited shock from her family [1], with her brother releasing a statement saying, "She's not an object" [2]. The family has also made a public plea for the President to ensure Epstein's accomplice, Ghislaine Maxwell, remains in prison [3]. **July 26, 2025**

**OVERVIEW**

This briefing synthesizes intelligence from today’s news cycle to provide an objective, non-partisan analysis of the most urgent political, economic, and national security developments. ### **Area 1: Economic & Trade Policy**

**Topic 1.1: Administration Implements Sweeping New Global Tariffs**

The Trump administration is executing a significant realignment of U.S. trade policy, centered on a new executive order imposing global tariff rates effective August 7 [1]. This action, which delayed the previous deadline, has injected a fresh wave of uncertainty into the global economy [2]. Core to the new policy is a steep 40% duty on all transshipped goods, designed to counter circumvention [3]. The White House has released a comprehensive list of new rates for dozens of countries, resulting in a "tariff shock" for key partners. Switzerland, for example, now faces an unexpected 39% U.S. tariff, highlighting the disruptive scale of the changes [4]. One major editorial board has characterized the new tariff regime as "both a political and an economic threat" [5].

Switzerland, for example, now faces an unexpected 39% U.S. tariff, highlighting the disruptive scale of the changes [4]. One major editorial board has characterized the new tariff regime as "both a political and an economic threat" [5].
